<p><b>Essen</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈʔɛsn̩]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Essen.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/De-Essen.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Essen.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>: <i>Assindia</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">city</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>, Germany. Its population of approximately 589,000 (as of 31 March 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) makes it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_by_population" title="List of cities in Germany by population">ninth-largest city in Germany</a>. It is the central city of the northern (<a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a>) part of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> metropolitan area and seat to several of the region's authorities. Essen is seat to 13 of the 100 largest German corporations, including three <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a> corporations, placing the city second only to <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and on-par with <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt am Main</a> in number of corporate headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Founded around 845, Essen remained a small town within the sphere of influence of an important <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Abbey" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Abbey">ecclesiastical principality</a> (<a href="/wiki/Essen_Abbey" title="Essen Abbey">Essen Abbey</a>) until the onset of industrialization. The city then — especially through the <a href="/wiki/Krupp" title="Krupp">Krupp</a> family iron works — became one of Germany's most important coal and steel centers. Essen, until the 1970s, attracted workers from all over the country; it was the 5th-largest city in Germany between 1929 and 1988, peaking at over 730,000 inhabitants in 1962. Following the region-wide decline of heavy industries in the last decades of the 20th century, the city has seen the development of a strong <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">tertiary sector of the economy</a>.</p>
<p>Although it is the (in total) most <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">indebted</a> city in Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Essen continues to pursue its redevelopment plans. Notable accomplishments in recent years include the title of <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> on behalf of the whole Ruhr area in 2010 and the selection as the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital" class="mw-redirect" title="European Green Capital">European Green Capital</a> for 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1958, Essen was chosen to serve as the seat to a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Essen" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Essen">Roman Catholic diocese</a> (often referred to as <i>Ruhrbistum</i> or <i>diocese of the Ruhr</i>). In early 2003, the universities of Essen and the nearby city of <a href="/wiki/Duisburg" title="Duisburg">Duisburg</a> (both established in 1972) were merged into the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Duisburg-Essen" title="University of Duisburg-Essen">University of Duisburg-Essen</a> with campuses in both cities and a <a href="/wiki/University_hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="University hospital">university hospital</a> in Essen.</p>
<p></p>

<p>Essen is located in the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> area, one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a> in Europe (see also: <a href="/wiki/Megalopolis_(city_type)" class="mw-redirect" title="Megalopolis (city type)">megalopolis</a>), comprising eleven <a href="/wiki/Independent_city" title="Independent city">independent cities</a> and four <a href="/wiki/District" title="District">districts</a> with some 5.3 million inhabitants. The city limits of Essen itself are 87&#160;km (54&#160;mi) long and border ten cities, five independent and five <i>kreisangehörig</i> (i.e., belonging to a district), with a total population of approximately 1.4 million. The city extends over 21&#160;km (13&#160;mi) from north to south and 17&#160;km (11&#160;mi) from west to east, mainly north of the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_(river)" title="Ruhr (river)">River Ruhr</a>.</p>
<p>The Ruhr forms the <i>Lake Baldeney</i> <a href="/wiki/Reservoir" title="Reservoir">reservoir</a> in the boroughs of Fischlaken, Kupferdreh, Heisingen and <a href="/wiki/Essen-Werden" title="Essen-Werden">Werden</a>. The lake, a popular recreational area, dates from 1931 to 1933, when some thousands of unemployed <a href="/wiki/Coal_miner" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal miner">coal miners</a> dredged it with primitive tools. Generally, large areas south of the River Ruhr (including the suburbs of Schuir and <a href="/wiki/Kettwig" title="Kettwig">Kettwig</a>) are quite green and are often quoted as examples of rural structures in the otherwise relatively densely populated central Ruhr area. According to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Statistical_Office_of_Germany" title="Federal Statistical Office of Germany">Federal Statistical Office of Germany</a>, Essen with 9.2% of its area covered by recreational green is the greenest city in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> and the third-greenest city in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The city has been shortlisted for the title of <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital" class="mw-redirect" title="European Green Capital">European Green Capital</a> two consecutive times, for 2016 and 2017, winning for 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The city was singled out for its exemplary practices in protecting and enhancing nature and biodiversity and efforts to reduce water consumption. Essen participates in a variety of networks and initiatives to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and to improve the city’s resilience in the face of climate change.</p>
<p>The lowest point can be found in the northern borough of Karnap at 26.5&#160;m (86.9&#160;ft), the highest point in the borough of Heidhausen at 202.5&#160;m (664&#160;ft). The average elevation is 116&#160;m (381&#160;ft).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_districts">City districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: City districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Essen comprises fifty boroughs which in turn are grouped into nine suburban districts (called <i><a href="/wiki/Stadtbezirk" title="Stadtbezirk">Stadtbezirke</a></i>) often named after the most important boroughs. Each Stadtbezirk is assigned a <a href="/wiki/Roman_numeral" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman numeral">Roman numeral</a> and has a local body of nineteen members with limited authority. Most of the boroughs were originally independent municipalities but were gradually annexed from 1901 to 1975. This long-lasting process of annexation has led to a strong identification of the population with "their" boroughs or districts and to a rare peculiarity: The borough of <a href="/wiki/Kettwig" title="Kettwig">Kettwig</a>, located south of the Ruhr River, and which was not annexed until 1975, has its own <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">area code</a>. Additionally (allegedly due to relatively high church tax incomes), the Archbishop of Cologne managed to keep Kettwig directly subject to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Cologne" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Cologne">Archdiocese of Cologne</a>, whereas all other boroughs of Essen and some neighboring cities constitute the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Essen" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Essen">Diocese of Essen</a>.</p>
<dl>
<dd><i>For a list of all boroughs of the city, see the section <a href="#boroughs">Boroughs of Essen</a> below.</i></dd>
</dl>

<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Despite its industrial history, Essen is generally regarded as one of Germany's greenest cities.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The picture shows the borough of <a href="/wiki/Kettwig" title="Kettwig">Kettwig</a>, annexed in 1975.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Essen has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a>–<a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Oceanic climate</a> with relatively mild winters and cool summers. Its average annual temperature is 10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F): 13.3&#160;°C (56&#160;°F) during the day and 6.7&#160;°C (44&#160;°F) at night. The average annual precipitation is 934&#160;mm (37&#160;in). The coldest month of the year is January, when the average temperature is 2.4&#160;°C (36&#160;°F). The warmest months are July and August, with an average temperature of 18&#160;°C (64&#160;°F). The record high is 36.6&#160;°C (98&#160;°F) and the record low is −24&#160;°C (−11&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Essen" title="Timeline of Essen">Timeline of Essen</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Essen-Kupferstich-Merian.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Essen-Kupferstich-Merian.png/300px-Essen-Kupferstich-Merian.png" width="300" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Essen-Kupferstich-Merian.png/450px-Essen-Kupferstich-Merian.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Essen-Kupferstich-Merian.png/600px-Essen-Kupferstich-Merian.png 2x" data-file-width="2514" data-file-height="858" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Essen-Kupferstich-Merian.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Essen on an engraving from 1647</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_name">Origin of the name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Origin of the name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In German-speaking countries, the name of the city Essen often causes confusion as to its origins, because it is commonly known as the German <a href="/wiki/Infinitive" title="Infinitive">infinitive</a> of the <a href="/wiki/German_verbs" title="German verbs">verb</a> for "eating" (written as lowercase <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/essen" class="extiw" title="wikt:essen">essen</a></i>), and/or the German <a href="/wiki/German_nouns" title="German nouns">noun</a> for <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">food</a> (which is always <a href="/wiki/Capitalization" title="Capitalization">capitalized</a> as <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Essen" class="extiw" title="wikt:Essen">Essen</a></i>, adding to the confusion). Although scholars still dispute the interpretation of the name,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> there remain a few noteworthy interpretations. The oldest known form of the city's name is <i>Astnide</i>, which changed to Essen by way of forms such as Astnidum, Assinde, Essendia and Esnede. The name Astnide may have referred either to a region where many <a href="/wiki/Ash_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Ash tree">ash trees</a> were found or to a region in the East (of the <a href="/wiki/Frankish_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankish Empire">Frankish Empire</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a> word for fireplace, Esse, is also commonly mentioned due to the industrial history of the city, but is highly unlikely since the old forms of the city name originate from times before industrialization.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The oldest archaeological find, the <i><a href="/wiki/Vogelheimer_Klinge" title="Vogelheimer Klinge">Vogelheimer Klinge</a></i>, dates back to 280,000 – 250,000 BC. It is a <a href="/wiki/Blade" title="Blade">blade</a> found in the borough of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vogelheim&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vogelheim (page does not exist)">Vogelheim</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vogelheim" class="extiw" title="de:Vogelheim">de</a>)</span> in the northern part of the city during the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine%E2%80%93Herne_Canal" title="Rhine–Herne Canal">Rhine–Herne Canal</a> in 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Other artifacts from the <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> have also been found, although these are not overly numerous. Land utilization was very high – especially due to mining activities during the Industrial Age – and any more major finds, especially from the <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> era, are not expected. Finds from 3,000 BC and onwards are far more common, the most important one being a <a href="/wiki/Megalith" title="Megalith">Megalithic tomb</a> found in 1937. Simply called Steinkiste (Chest of Stone), it is referred to as "Essen's earliest preserved example of architecture".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Essen was part of the settlement areas of several Germanic peoples (<a href="/wiki/Chatti" title="Chatti">Chatti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bructeri" title="Bructeri">Bructeri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marsi_(Germanic)" title="Marsi (Germanic)">Marsi</a>), although a clear distinction among these groupings is difficult.</p>
<p>The Alteburg castle in the south of Essen dates back to the 1st or 2nd century BC, the Herrenburg to the 8th century <a href="/wiki/AD" class="mw-redirect" title="AD">AD</a>.</p>
<p>Recent research into <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Geography_(Ptolemy)" title="Geography (Ptolemy)">Geographia</a></i> has identified the <i>polis</i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Oppidum" title="Oppidum">oppidum</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Navalia" title="Navalia">Navalia</a> as Essen.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="8th–12th_centuries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="8th.E2.80.9312th_centuries">8th–12th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 8th–12th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Essen_2011_66-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Essen_2011_66-2.jpg/220px-Essen_2011_66-2.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Essen_2011_66-2.jpg/330px-Essen_2011_66-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Essen_2011_66-2.jpg/440px-Essen_2011_66-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3293" data-file-height="2569" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Essen_2011_66-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Essen_Minster" title="Essen Minster">Essen Minster</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Around 845, Saint <a href="/wiki/Altfrid" title="Altfrid">Altfrid</a> (around 800–874), the later <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Hildesheim" title="Bishopric of Hildesheim">Bishop of Hildesheim</a>, founded an abbey for women (<i>coenobium Astnide</i>) in the centre of present-day Essen. The first abbess was Altfrid's relative Gerswit (see also: <a href="/wiki/Essen_Abbey" title="Essen Abbey">Essen Abbey</a>). In 799, <a href="/wiki/Liudger" class="mw-redirect" title="Liudger">Saint Liudger</a> had already founded <a href="/wiki/Benedictine_Order" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedictine Order">Benedictine</a> <a href="/wiki/Werden_Abbey" title="Werden Abbey">Werden Abbey</a> on its own grounds a few kilometers south. The region was sparsely populated with only a few <a href="/wiki/Smallholding" title="Smallholding">smallholdings</a> and an old and probably abandoned castle. Whereas Werden Abbey sought to support Liudger's missionary work in the <a href="/wiki/Harz" title="Harz">Harz</a> region (<a href="/wiki/Helmstedt" title="Helmstedt">Helmstedt</a>/<a href="/wiki/Halberstadt" title="Halberstadt">Halberstadt</a>), Essen Abbey was meant to care for women of the higher <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxon</a> nobility. This abbey was not an abbey in the ordinary sense, but rather intended as a residence and educational institution for the daughters and widows of the higher nobility; led by an abbess, the members other than the abbess herself were not obliged to take vows of <a href="/wiki/Chastity" title="Chastity">chastity</a>.</p>
<p>Around 852, construction of the collegiate church of the abbey began, to be completed in 870. A major fire in 946 heavily damaged both the church and the settlement. The church was rebuilt, expanded considerably, and is the foundation of the present Essen Cathedral.</p>
<p>The first documented mention of Essen dates back to 898, when <a href="/wiki/Zwentibold" title="Zwentibold">Zwentibold</a>, King of <a href="/wiki/Lotharingia" title="Lotharingia">Lotharingia</a>, willed territory on the western bank of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">River Rhine</a> to the abbey. Another document, describing the foundation of the abbey and allegedly dating back to 870, is now considered an 11th-century forgery.</p>
<p>In 971, <a href="/wiki/Mathilde,_Abbess_of_Essen" title="Mathilde, Abbess of Essen">Mathilde II</a>, granddaughter of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Otto_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto I, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto I</a>, took charge of the abbey. She was to become the most important of all abbesses in the history of Essen. She reigned for over 40 years, and endowed the abbey's treasury with invaluable objects such as the oldest preserved seven branched candelabrum, and the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Madonna_of_Essen" title="Golden Madonna of Essen">Golden Madonna of Essen</a>, the oldest known <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(art)" title="Madonna (art)">sculpture of the Virgin Mary</a> in the western world. Mathilde was succeeded by other women related to the <a href="/wiki/Ottonian" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottonian">Ottonian</a> emperors: Sophia, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Otto_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto II, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto II</a> and sister of <a href="/wiki/Otto_III,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto III, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto III</a>, and Teophanu, granddaughter of Otto II. It was under the reign of Teophanu that Essen, which had been called a city since 1003, received the right to hold markets in 1041. Ten years later, Teophanu had the eastern part of Essen Abbey constructed. Its <a href="/wiki/Crypt" title="Crypt">crypt</a> contains the tombs of St. Altfrid, Mathilde II, and Teophanu herself.</p>
<h3><span id="13th–17th_centuries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="13th.E2.80.9317th_centuries">13th–17th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 13th–17th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Altessen,_Weltladen_Alte_Kirche_foto3_2012-08-19_12.43.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Altessen%2C_Weltladen_Alte_Kirche_foto3_2012-08-19_12.43.jpg/170px-Altessen%2C_Weltladen_Alte_Kirche_foto3_2012-08-19_12.43.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Altessen%2C_Weltladen_Alte_Kirche_foto3_2012-08-19_12.43.jpg/255px-Altessen%2C_Weltladen_Alte_Kirche_foto3_2012-08-19_12.43.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Altessen%2C_Weltladen_Alte_Kirche_foto3_2012-08-19_12.43.jpg/340px-Altessen%2C_Weltladen_Alte_Kirche_foto3_2012-08-19_12.43.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3268" data-file-height="4357" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Altessen,_Weltladen_Alte_Kirche_foto3_2012-08-19_12.43.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alte Kirche (Old Church, built 1887), Altenessen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1216, the abbey, which had only been an important landowner until then, gained the status of a princely residence when Emperor <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick II</a> called abbess Elisabeth I <i>Reichsfürstin</i> (<i>Princess of the Empire</i>) in an official letter. In 1244, 28 years later, Essen received its town charter and seal when <a href="/wiki/Konrad_von_Hochstaden" title="Konrad von Hochstaden">Konrad von Hochstaden</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Cologne" title="Archbishop of Cologne">Archbishop of Cologne</a>, marched into the city and erected a city wall together with the population. This proved a temporary emancipation of the population of the city from the princess-abbesses, but this lasted only until 1290. That year, King <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_I_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Rudolph I of Germany">Rudolph I</a> restored the princess-abbesses to full sovereignty over the city, much to the dismay of the population of the growing city, who called for self-administration and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_immediacy" title="Imperial immediacy">imperial immediacy</a>. The title <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">free imperial city</a> was finally granted by Emperor <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles IV</a> in 1377. However, in 1372, Charles had paradoxically endorsed Rudolph I's 1290 decision and hence left both the abbey and the city in imperial favour. Disputes between the city and the abbey about supremacy over the region remained common until the abbey's dissolution in 1803. Many lawsuits were filed at the <a href="/wiki/Reichskammergericht" title="Reichskammergericht">Reichskammergericht</a>, one of them lasting almost 200 years. The final decision of the court in 1670 was that the city had to be "duly obedient in dos and don'ts" to the abbesses but could maintain its old rights—a decision that did not really solve any of the problems.</p>
<p>In 1563, the city council, with its self-conception as the only legitimate ruler of Essen, introduced the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>. The Catholic abbey had no troops to counter this development.</p>
<h3><span id="Thirty_Years'_War"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Thirty_Years.27_War">Thirty Years' War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Thirty Years' War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, the Protestant city and the Catholic abbey opposed each other. In 1623, princess-abbess Maria Clara von Spaur, Pflaum und Valör, managed to direct Catholic Spaniards against the city in order to initiate a <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a>. In 1624, a "re-Catholicization" law was enacted, and churchgoing was strictly controlled. In 1628, the city council filed against this at the Reichskammergericht. Maria had to flee to Cologne when the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> stormed the city in 1629. She returned in the summer of 1631 following the <a href="/wiki/Bavarians" title="Bavarians">Bavarians</a> under <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Heinrich_Graf_zu_Pappenheim" title="Gottfried Heinrich Graf zu Pappenheim">Gottfried Heinrich Graf zu Pappenheim</a>, only to leave again in September. She died 1644 in Cologne.</p>
<p>The war proved a severe blow to the city, with frequent arrests, kidnapping and rape. Even after the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a> from 1648, troops remained in the city until 9 September 1650.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrialisation">Industrialisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Industrialisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Drei_Ringe_von_Krupp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Drei_Ringe_von_Krupp.jpg/170px-Drei_Ringe_von_Krupp.jpg" width="170" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Drei_Ringe_von_Krupp.jpg/255px-Drei_Ringe_von_Krupp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Drei_Ringe_von_Krupp.jpg/340px-Drei_Ringe_von_Krupp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="428" data-file-height="412" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Drei_Ringe_von_Krupp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The three rings of Krupp</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Essen,_Stammhaus_Krupp,_2014-11_CN-02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Essen%2C_Stammhaus_Krupp%2C_2014-11_CN-02.jpg/220px-Essen%2C_Stammhaus_Krupp%2C_2014-11_CN-02.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Essen%2C_Stammhaus_Krupp%2C_2014-11_CN-02.jpg/330px-Essen%2C_Stammhaus_Krupp%2C_2014-11_CN-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Essen%2C_Stammhaus_Krupp%2C_2014-11_CN-02.jpg/440px-Essen%2C_Stammhaus_Krupp%2C_2014-11_CN-02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4581" data-file-height="3034" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Essen,_Stammhaus_Krupp,_2014-11_CN-02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Historic House of the Krupp Family</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first historic evidence of the important mining tradition of Essen date back to the 14th century, when the princess-abbess was granted mining rights. The first silver mine opened in 1354, but the indisputably more important coal was not mentioned until 1371, and coal mining only began in 1450.</p>
<p>At the end of the 16th century, many coal mines had opened in Essen, and the city earned a name as a centre of the weapons industry. Around 1570, <a href="/wiki/Gunsmith" title="Gunsmith">gunsmiths</a> made high profits and in 1620, they produced 14,000 rifles and pistols a year. The city became increasingly important strategically.</p>
<p>Resident in Essen since the 16th century, the Krupp family dynasty and Essen shaped each other. In 1811, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Krupp" title="Friedrich Krupp">Friedrich Krupp</a> founded Germany's first cast-steel factory in Essen and laid the cornerstone for what was to be the largest enterprise in Europe for a couple of decades. The weapon factories in Essen became so important that a sign facing the <a href="/wiki/Essen_Hauptbahnhof" title="Essen Hauptbahnhof">main railway station</a> welcomed visitor <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> to the "Armory of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Reich</a>" in 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The Krupp Works also were the main reason for the <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bild:Essen_Bevoelkerungsentwicklung_01_KMJ.png" class="extiw" title="de:Bild:Essen Bevoelkerungsentwicklung 01 KMJ.png">large population growth</a> beginning in the mid-19th century. Essen reached a population of 100,000 in 1896. Other industrialists, such as Friedrich Grillo, who in 1892 donated the <a href="/wiki/Grillo-Theater" title="Grillo-Theater">Grillo-Theater</a> to the city, also played a major role in the shaping of the city and the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> area in the late 19th and early 20th century.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_World_War">First World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: First World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Riots broke out in February 1917 following a breakdown in the supply of flour. There were then strikes in the Krupp factory.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupation_of_the_Ruhr">Occupation of the Ruhr</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Occupation of the Ruhr">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On January 11, 1923, the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Ruhr" title="Occupation of the Ruhr">Occupation of the Ruhr</a> was carried out by the invasion of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgian</a> troops into the Ruhr. The French Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Poincar%C3%A9" title="Raymond Poincaré">Raymond Poincaré</a> was convinced that Germany failed to comply the demands of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>. On the morning of March 31, 1923 it came to the sad culmination of this French-German confrontation.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> A small French military command, occupied the Krupp car hall to seize several vehicles. This event called 13 deaths and 28 injured. The occupation of the Ruhr ended in summer 1925.</p>
<h3><span id="Phase_of_the_Nazi_seizure_of_power_in_1933–34"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_of_the_Nazi_seizure_of_power_in_1933.E2.80.9334">Phase of the Nazi seizure of power in 1933–34</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Phase of the Nazi seizure of power in 1933–34">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Heinrich Maria Martin Schäfer was appointed <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> of Essen on December 21, 1932. After the Nazi seizure of power Theodor Reismann-Grone became on April 5, 1933 the mayor. Essen was then divided in 27 local NSDAP groups (NSDAP-Ortsgruppe).<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1938_November_Pogrom">1938 November Pogrom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 1938 November Pogrom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On the night of 10 November 1938, the <a href="/wiki/Old_Synagogue,_Essen" title="Old Synagogue, Essen">synagogue</a> was sacked, but remained through the whole war in the exterior almost intact.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Steele,_Germany" title="Steele, Germany">Steele</a> synagogue was completely destroyed.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forced_labor_camps_and_concentration_camps">Forced labor camps and concentration camps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Forced labor camps and concentration camps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tens of thousands of forced laborers arrived in the Nazi era in 350 Essen camps, forced to <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II" title="Forced labour under German rule during World War II">Forced labour under German rule during World War II</a> at companies like Krupp, Siemens and for mining work.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In Essen there were in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a> several <a href="/wiki/Subcamp_(SS)" title="Subcamp (SS)">Subcamps</a> as the ssub camp<i>Humboldtstraße</i>, the <i>Gelsenberg</i> ssub campand the subcamp <i>Schwarze Poth</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-941,_Essen,_zerst%C3%B6rte_Krupp-Werke,_Luftaufnahme.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-941%2C_Essen%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Krupp-Werke%2C_Luftaufnahme.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-941%2C_Essen%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Krupp-Werke%2C_Luftaufnahme.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-941%2C_Essen%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Krupp-Werke%2C_Luftaufnahme.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-941%2C_Essen%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Krupp-Werke%2C_Luftaufnahme.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-941%2C_Essen%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Krupp-Werke%2C_Luftaufnahme.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-941%2C_Essen%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Krupp-Werke%2C_Luftaufnahme.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="590" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-941,_Essen,_zerst%C3%B6rte_Krupp-Werke,_Luftaufnahme.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Devastation of Krupp factory</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As a major industrial centre, Essen was a target for <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">allied</a> bombing, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> (RAF) dropping a total of 36,429 <a href="/wiki/Long_tons" class="mw-redirect" title="Long tons">long tons</a> of bombs on the city.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Over 270 air raids were launched against the city, destroying 90% of the centre and 60% of the suburbs.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> On 5 March 1943 Essen was subjected to one of the heaviest air-raids of the war. 461 people were killed, 1,593 injured and a further 50,000 residents of Essen were made homeless.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> On 13 December 1944 three British <a href="/wiki/Airman" title="Airman">airmen</a> were lynched.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Krupp" title="Krupp">Krupp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Essen_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Essen in World War II">Bombing of Essen in World War II</a></div>
<p>The Allied ground advance into Germany reached Essen in April 1945. The US <a href="/wiki/507th_Infantry_Regiment_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="507th Infantry Regiment (United States)">507th Parachute Infantry Regiment</a> of the <a href="/wiki/17th_Airborne_Division_(United_States)" title="17th Airborne Division (United States)">17th Airborne Division</a>, acting as regular infantry and not in a parachute role, entered the city unopposed and captured it on 10 April 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Under_British_occupation">Under British occupation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Under British occupation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the successful invasion of Germany by the allies, Essen was assigned to the <a href="/wiki/British_Zone_of_Occupation" class="mw-redirect" title="British Zone of Occupation">British Zone of Occupation</a>. On 8 March 1946, a German Army Officer and a civilian were hanged for the lynching of three British Airmen in December 1944.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twenty-first_century">Twenty-first century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Twenty-first century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Essen_pan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Essen_pan.jpg/220px-Essen_pan.jpg" width="220" height="75" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Essen_pan.jpg/330px-Essen_pan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Essen_pan.jpg/440px-Essen_pan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1564" data-file-height="532" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Essen_pan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View over Central Essen from <a href="/wiki/Bottrop" title="Bottrop">Bottrop</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although no weaponry is produced in Essen any more, old industrial enterprises such as <a href="/wiki/ThyssenKrupp" title="ThyssenKrupp">ThyssenKrupp</a> and <a href="/wiki/RWE" title="RWE">RWE</a> remain large employers in the city. Foundations such as the <a href="/wiki/Alfried_Krupp_von_Bohlen_und_Halbach" title="Alfried Krupp von Bohlen und Halbach">Alfried Krupp von Bohlen und Halbach</a>-<a href="/wiki/Stiftung" title="Stiftung">Stiftung</a> still promote the well-being of the city, for example by supporting a hospital and donating €55,000,000 for a new building for the <a href="/wiki/Museum_Folkwang" title="Museum Folkwang">Museum Folkwang</a>, one of the Ruhr area's major art museums.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Muenster_Rathaus_Essen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Muenster_Rathaus_Essen.jpg/220px-Muenster_Rathaus_Essen.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Muenster_Rathaus_Essen.jpg/330px-Muenster_Rathaus_Essen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Muenster_Rathaus_Essen.jpg/440px-Muenster_Rathaus_Essen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Muenster_Rathaus_Essen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old and new government seats: Essen Cathedral (front) and the <a href="/wiki/Essen_City_Hall" title="Essen City Hall">city hall</a> (background)</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_development">Historical development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Historical development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The administration of Essen had for a long time been in the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Princess-abbess" class="mw-redirect" title="Princess-abbess">princess-abbesses</a> as heads of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Abbey" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Abbey">Imperial Abbey</a> of <a href="/wiki/Essen_Abbey" title="Essen Abbey">Essen</a>. However, from the 14th century onwards, the <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">city council</a> increasingly grew in importance. In 1335, it started choosing two <a href="/wiki/Burgomaster" title="Burgomaster">burgomasters</a>, one of whom was placed in charge of the treasury. In 1377, Essen was granted <a href="/wiki/Imperial_immediacy" title="Imperial immediacy">imperial immediacy</a><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> but had to abandon this privilege later on. Between the early 15th and 20th centuries, the political system of Essen underwent several changes, most importantly the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> in 1563, the <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexation</a> of 1802 by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a>, and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Secularization" title="Secularization">secularization</a> of the principality in 1803. The territory was made part of the Prussian <a href="/wiki/Province_of_J%C3%BClich-Cleves-Berg" title="Province of Jülich-Cleves-Berg">Province of Jülich-Cleves-Berg</a> from 1815 to 1822, after which it became part of the Prussian <a href="/wiki/Rhine_Province" title="Rhine Province">Rhine Province</a> until its dissolution in 1946.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/German_Revolution_of_1918%E2%80%9319" title="German Revolution of 1918–19">German Revolution of 1918–19</a>, Essen was the home of the Essen Tendency (Essener Richtung) within the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Workers%27_Party_of_Germany" title="Communist Workers' Party of Germany">Communist Workers' Party of Germany</a>. In 1922 they founded the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Workers%27_International" title="Communist Workers' International">Communist Workers' International</a>. Essen became one of the centres of resistance to <a href="/wiki/Social_Democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Democracy">Social Democracy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Freikorps" title="Freikorps">Freikorps</a> alike.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi</a> era (1933–1945), mayors were installed by the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the military government of the <a href="/wiki/British_occupation_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="British occupation zone">British occupation zone</a> installed a new mayor and a municipal constitution modeled on that of British cities. Later, the city council was again elected by the population. The mayor was elected by the council as its head and as the city's main <a href="/wiki/Representation_(politics)" title="Representation (politics)">representative</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">administration</a> was led by a full-time <i>Oberstadtdirektor</i>. In 1999, the position of Oberstadtdirektor was abolished in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a> and the mayor became both main representative and administrative head. In addition, the population now elects the mayor directly.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_council">City council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: City council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>The city is governed by a coalition of SPD and CDU.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DEU_Essen_COA.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/DEU_Essen_COA.svg/170px-DEU_Essen_COA.svg.png" width="170" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/DEU_Essen_COA.svg/255px-DEU_Essen_COA.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/DEU_Essen_COA.svg/340px-DEU_Essen_COA.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="776" data-file-height="717" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DEU_Essen_COA.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Essen's coat of arms</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hotel_Handelshof_Essen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hotel_Handelshof_Essen.jpg/220px-Hotel_Handelshof_Essen.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hotel_Handelshof_Essen.jpg/330px-Hotel_Handelshof_Essen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hotel_Handelshof_Essen.jpg/440px-Hotel_Handelshof_Essen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2249" data-file-height="1619" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hotel_Handelshof_Essen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Handelshof Hotel with modified coat of arms and unofficial motto</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The coat of arms of the city of Essen is a heraldic peculiarity. Granted in 1886, it is a so-called <i>Allianzwappen</i> (<i>arms of alliance</i>) and consists of two separate shields under a single crown. Most other coats of arms of cities show a wall instead of a crown. The crown, however, does not refer to the city of Essen itself, but instead to the <a href="/wiki/German_Mediatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="German Mediatisation">secularized</a> <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">ecclesiastical principality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Essen_Abbey" title="Essen Abbey">Essen</a> under the reign of the princess-abbesses. The dexter (heraldically right) <a href="/wiki/Escutcheon_(heraldry)" title="Escutcheon (heraldry)">escutcheon</a> shows the double-headed Imperial Eagle of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, granted to the city in 1623. The sinister (heraldically left) escutcheon is one of the oldest emblems of Essen and shows a sword that people believed was used to behead the city's <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron</a> <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cosmas_and_Damian" title="Saints Cosmas and Damian">Saints Cosmas and Damian</a>. People tend to connect the sword in the left shield with one found in the Cathedral Treasury. This sword, however, is much more recent.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> A slightly modified and more heraldically correct version of the coat of arms can be found on the roof of the <i>Handelshof</i> hotel near the main station.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Germany" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany">List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany</a></div>
<p>Essen is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:<sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grenoble" title="Grenoble">Grenoble</a>, France <small><i>(since 1974)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nizhny_Novgorod" title="Nizhny Novgorod">Nizhny Novgorod</a>, Russia <small><i>(since 1991)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/City_of_Sunderland" title="City of Sunderland">City of Sunderland</a>, United Kingdom <small><i>(since 1949)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tampere" title="Tampere">Tampere</a>, Finland <small><i>(since 1960)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>, Israel <small><i>(since 1991)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Monessen,_Pennsylvania" title="Monessen, Pennsylvania">City of Monessen, Pennsylvania</a>, situated along the <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_River" title="Monongahela River">Monongahela River</a>, was named after the river and Essen.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are cooperations with the following cities:<sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Erfurt" title="Erfurt">Erfurt</a>, Germany <small><i>(since 1991)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zabrze" title="Zabrze">Zabrze</a>, Poland <small><i>(since 2008)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Qingdao" title="Qingdao">Quingdao</a>, China <small><i>(since 2008)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-RuhrTwins2010_33-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RuhrTwins2010-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_infrastructure">Industry and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Industry and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Essen is home to several large companies, among them the <a href="/wiki/ThyssenKrupp" title="ThyssenKrupp">ThyssenKrupp</a> industrial conglomerate which is also registered in <a href="/wiki/Duisburg" title="Duisburg">Duisburg</a> and originates from a 1999 merger between Duisburg-based <i>Thyssen AG</i> and Essen-based <a href="/wiki/Krupp" title="Krupp">Friedrich Krupp AG Hoesch-Krupp</a>. The largest company registered only in Essen is Germany's second-largest <a href="/wiki/Electric_utility" title="Electric utility">electric utility</a> <a href="/wiki/RWE" title="RWE">RWE AG</a>. Essen also hosts parts of the corporate headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Schenker_AG" title="Schenker AG">Schenker AG</a>, the logistics division of Deutsche Bahn. Other major companies include Germany's largest construction company <a href="/wiki/Hochtief_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Hochtief AG">Hochtief AG</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Aldi" title="Aldi">Aldi Nord</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evonik_Industries" title="Evonik Industries">Evonik Industries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karstadt" title="Karstadt">Karstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medion" title="Medion">Medion AG</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deichmann_SE" title="Deichmann SE">Deichmann</a>, Europe's largest shoe retailer. <a href="/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="The Coca-Cola Company">The Coca-Cola Company</a> had also originally established their German headquarters in Essen (around 1930), where it remained until 2003, when it was moved to the capital Berlin. In light of the <a href="/wiki/Energy_transition_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy transition in Germany">Energy transition in Germany</a>, Germany's largest <a href="/wiki/Electric_utility" title="Electric utility">electric utility</a> <a href="/wiki/E.ON" title="E.ON">E.ON</a> announced that, after restructuring and splitting off its conventional electricity generation division (coal, gas, atomic energy), it will also move its headquarters to Essen in 2016, becoming a sole provider of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Further the chemical distribution company <a href="/wiki/Brenntag" title="Brenntag">Brenntag</a> announced to move its headquarter to Essen end of 2017.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fairs">Fairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Fairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city's exhibition centre, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Messe_Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Messe Essen (page does not exist)">Messe Essen</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Messe_Essen" class="extiw" title="de:Messe Essen">de</a>)</span>, hosts some 50 <a href="/wiki/Trade_fair" title="Trade fair">trade fairs</a> each year. With around 530.000 visitors each year, <a href="/wiki/Essen_Motor_Show" title="Essen Motor Show">Essen Motor Show</a> is by far the largest event held there. It has been described as "the showcase event of the year for the tuning community"<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and as the German version of the annual <a href="/wiki/SEMA" title="SEMA">SEMA</a> auto show in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> As contrasted with the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Auto_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt Auto Show">Frankfurt Auto Show</a>, the Essen show is smaller and is focused on <a href="/wiki/Car_tuning" title="Car tuning">car tuning</a> and racing interests.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>Other important fairs open to consumers include <a href="/wiki/SPIEL" class="mw-redirect" title="SPIEL">SPIEL</a>, the world's biggest consumer fair for gaming, and one of the leading fairs for <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian sports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equitana" title="Equitana">Equitana</a>, held every two years. Important fairs restricted to professionals include "Security" (security and fire protection), IPM (gardening) and E-World (energy and water).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Westdeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Westdeutscher Rundfunk">Westdeutscher Rundfunk</a> has a studio in Essen, which is responsible for the central <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> area. Each day, it produces a 30-minute regional evening news magazine (called <i>Lokalzeit Ruhr</i>), a 5-minute afternoon news programme, and several radio news programmes. A local broadcasting station went on air in the late 1990s. The <a href="/wiki/WAZ-Mediengruppe" class="mw-redirect" title="WAZ-Mediengruppe">WAZ Media Group</a> is one of the most important (print) media companies in Europe and publishes the Ruhr area's two most important daily newspapers, <i><a href="/wiki/Westdeutsche_Allgemeine_Zeitung" title="Westdeutsche Allgemeine Zeitung">Westdeutsche Allgemeine Zeitung</a></i> (WAZ; 580,000 copies) and <i>Neue Ruhr/Rhein Zeitung</i> (NRZ; 180,000 copies). In Essen, the WAZ Group also publishes the local <i>Borbecker Nachrichten</i> (at times Germany's largest local newspaper)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and <i>Werdener Nachrichten</i>, both of which had been independent weekly newspapers for parts of Essen. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Axel_Springer_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Axel Springer AG">Axel Springer</a> run a printing facility for their boulevard-style daily paper <i><a href="/wiki/Bild" title="Bild">Bild</a></i> in Essen.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One renowned educational institution in Essen is the <a href="/wiki/Folkwang_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Folkwang University">Folkwang University</a>, a university of the arts founded in 1927, which is headquartered in Essen and has additional facilities in Duisburg, <a href="/wiki/Bochum" title="Bochum">Bochum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>. Since 1927, its traditional main location has been in the former <a href="/wiki/Werden_Abbey" title="Werden Abbey">Werden Abbey</a> in Essen in the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr Area">Ruhr Area</a>, with additional facilities in <a href="/wiki/Duisburg" title="Duisburg">Duisburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bochum" title="Bochum">Bochum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>, and, since 2010, at the <a href="/wiki/Zollverein_Coal_Mine_Industrial_Complex" title="Zollverein Coal Mine Industrial Complex">Zeche Zollverein</a>, a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> also in Essen.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The Folkwang University is home to the international dance company <i>Folkwang Tanz Studio</i> (FTS). In 1963 the Folkwang school was renamed <i>Folkwang-Hochschule</i> (Folkwang Academy). In 2010 the institution began offering graduate studies and was renamed Folkwang University of the Arts. This coincided with <a href="/wiki/Ruhr.2010" title="Ruhr.2010">Ruhr.2010</a>, the festival in which the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> district was designated the <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> for the year 2010.</p>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Duisburg-Essen" title="University of Duisburg-Essen">University of Duisburg-Essen</a>, which resulted from a 2003 merger of the universities of Essen and Duisburg, is one of Germany's "youngest" universities with about 42,000 Students.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> One of its primary research areas is <i>urban systems</i> (i.e., sustainable development, logistics and transportation), a theme largely inspired by the highly urbanised Ruhr area. Other fields include <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Discrete_mathematics" title="Discrete mathematics">discrete mathematics</a> and "education in the 21st century". Another university in Essen is the private <i><a href="/wiki/Fachhochschule" title="Fachhochschule">Fachhochschule</a> für Ökonomie und Management</i>, a university of applied sciences with over 6,000 students and branches in 15 other major cities throughout Germany.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medicine">Medicine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Medicine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Essen offers a highly diversified health care system with more than 1,350 resident doctors and almost 6,000 beds in 13 hospitals, including a university hospital. The university hospital dates back to 1909, when the city council established a municipal hospital; although it was largely destroyed during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, it was later rebuilt, and finally gained the title of a university hospital in 1963. It focuses on <a href="/wiki/List_of_ICD-9_codes_390-459:_Diseases_of_the_circulatory_system#7._Diseases_of_the_circulatory_system_.28390.E2.80.93459.29" class="mw-redirect" title="List of ICD-9 codes 390-459: Diseases of the circulatory system">diseases of the circulatory system</a> (West German Heart Centre Essen), <a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">oncology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Organ_transplant" class="mw-redirect" title="Organ transplant">transplantation medicine</a>, with the department of <a href="/wiki/Bone_marrow_transplant" class="mw-redirect" title="Bone marrow transplant">bone marrow transplantation</a> being the second-largest of its kind in the world.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Streets_and_motorways">Streets and motorways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Streets and motorways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A40-Ruhrschnellweg-Huttrop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/A40-Ruhrschnellweg-Huttrop.jpg/220px-A40-Ruhrschnellweg-Huttrop.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/A40-Ruhrschnellweg-Huttrop.jpg/330px-A40-Ruhrschnellweg-Huttrop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/A40-Ruhrschnellweg-Huttrop.jpg/440px-A40-Ruhrschnellweg-Huttrop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1144" data-file-height="856" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A40-Ruhrschnellweg-Huttrop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_40" title="Bundesautobahn 40">Ruhrschnellweg</a> facing towards the <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a> of Essen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The road network of Essen consists of over 3,200 streets, which in total have a length of roughly 1,600&#160;km (994&#160;mi).</p>
<p>Three <i><a href="/wiki/German_Autobahnen" class="mw-redirect" title="German Autobahnen">Autobahnen</a></i> touch Essen territory, most importantly the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_40" title="Bundesautobahn 40">Ruhrschnellweg</a> (Ruhr expressway, A 40), which runs directly through the city, dividing it roughly in half. In a west-eastern direction, the A 40 connects the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Venlo" title="Venlo">Venlo</a> with Dortmund, running through the whole <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> area. It is one of the arterial roads of the Ruhr area (&gt; 140,000 vehicles/day) and suffers from heavy congestion during rush hours, which is why many people in the area nicknamed it <i>Ruhrschleichweg</i> (Ruhr crawling way). A tunnel was built in the 1970s, when the then-<a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe" title="Bundesstraße">Bundesstraße</a> was upgraded to <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">motorway</a> standards, so that the A 40 is hidden from public view in the inner-city district near the <a href="/wiki/Essen_Hauptbahnhof" title="Essen Hauptbahnhof">main railway station</a>.</p>
<p>In the north, the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_42" title="Bundesautobahn 42">A 42</a> briefly touches Essen territory, serving as an interconnection between the neighboring cities of <a href="/wiki/Oberhausen" title="Oberhausen">Oberhausen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gelsenkirchen" title="Gelsenkirchen">Gelsenkirchen</a> and destinations beyond.</p>
<p>A segment of the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_52" title="Bundesautobahn 52">A 52</a> connects Essen with the more southern region around <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>. On Essen territory, the A 52 runs from the southern boroughs near <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BClheim" title="Mülheim">Mülheim an der Ruhr</a> past the fairground and then merges with the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_40" title="Bundesautobahn 40">Ruhrschnellweg</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Autobahndreieck" class="mw-redirect" title="Autobahndreieck">Autobahndreieck</a> Essen-Ost junction east of the city centre.</p>
<p>With the A 40/A 52 in the southern parts of the city and the A 42 in the north, there is a gap in the motorway system often leading to congestion on streets leading from the central to the northern boroughs. An extension of the A 52 to connect the Essen-Ost junction with the A 42 to close this gap is considered urgent;<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> it has been planned for years but not yet been realized – most importantly due to the high-density areas this extension would lead through, resulting in high costs and concerns with the citizens.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As with most communes in the Ruhr area, local transport is carried out by a local, publicly owned company for transport within the city, the <a href="/wiki/DB_Regio" title="DB Regio">DB Regio</a> subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> for regional transport and Deutsche Bahn itself for long-distance journeys. The local carrier, Ruhrbahn, is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Verkehrsverbund_Rhein-Ruhr" title="Verkehrsverbund Rhein-Ruhr">Verkehrsverbund Rhein-Ruhr</a> (VRR) association of public transport companies in the Ruhr area, which provides a uniform fare structure in the whole region. Within the VRR region, tickets are valid on lines of all members as well as DB's <a href="/wiki/Railway_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway line">railway lines</a> (except the high-speed <a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">InterCity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">Intercity-Express</a> networks) and can be bought at ticket machines and service centres of Ruhrbahn, all other members of VRR, and DB.</p>
<p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Essen&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Ruhrbahn operates 3 U-<a href="/wiki/Stadtbahn" title="Stadtbahn">Stadtbahn</a> lines of the <a href="/wiki/Essen_Stadtbahn" title="Essen Stadtbahn">Essen Stadtbahn</a> network, 7 <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Essen" title="Trams in Essen">Straßenbahn (tram)</a> lines and 57 bus lines (16 of these serving as <i>Nacht Express</i> late-night lines only). The Stadtbahn and Straßenbahn operate on total route lengths of 19.6 kilometres (12.2&#160;mi) and 52.4 kilometres (32.6&#160;mi), respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> One tram line and a few bus lines coming from neighboring cities are operated by these cities' respective carriers. The U-Stadtbahn, which partly runs on used <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Light_Railway" title="Docklands Light Railway">Docklands Light Railway</a> stock, is a mixture of tram and full <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">underground</a> systems with 20 underground stations for the U-Stadtbahn and additional 4 underground stations used by the tram. Two lines of the U-Stadtbahn are completely intersection-free and hence independent from other traffic, and the U18 line leading from Mülheim main station to the <i>Bismarckplatz</i> station at the gates of the city centre partly runs above ground amidst the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_40" title="Bundesautobahn 40">A 40 motorway</a>. The Essen Stadtbahn is one of the Stadtbahn systems integrated into the greater <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr_Stadtbahn" title="Rhine-Ruhr Stadtbahn">Rhine-Ruhr Stadtbahn</a> network.</p>
